</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 302px"><div style="width: 302px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 300px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg/450px-Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg/675px-Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg/900px-Nave_of_the_Ste_C%C3%A9cile_Cathedral_-_2014-02-22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5117" data-file-height="3411" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Polychrome interior of <a href="/wiki/Albi_Cathedral" title="Albi Cathedral">Albi Cathedral</a> (1282–1480)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 198.66666666667px"><div style="width: 198.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 196.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg/295px-Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg" decoding="async" width="197" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg/443px-Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg/590px-Fa%C3%A7ade_de_la_cath%C3%A9drale_Saint-%C3%89tienne_de_Toulouse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5506" data-file-height="5599" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Toulouse_Cathedral" title="Toulouse Cathedral">Toulouse Cathedral</a> (13th century)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 302px"><div style="width: 302px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 300px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG/450px-Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG/675px-Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG/900px-Palmier_des_Jacobins.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The Palm Tree of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Jacobins" title="Church of the Jacobins">Jacobins church</a>, 28 meters high (<a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, 1292)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>From the 12th century onwards, the Gothic style spread from Northern France to other regions of France and gradually to the rest of the Europe. It was often carried by the highly skilled craftsmen who had trained in the Ile-de-France and then carried their crafts to other cities. The style was adapted to local styles and materials.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>, the new naves were usually very long, sometimes more than one hundred meters, and, from the long Romanesque tradition, the walls were thicker than in northern France, and had shorter buttresses. The interiors were narrower than in the north, and were given a strong sense of verticality by long and narrow bays and lancet arches. Rose windows were rare, replaced on the exterior by a large bay in <i>tiers point</i>. The facades had less sculptural decoration; decoration in the interior was largely in geometric forms. Norman Gothic also usually featured a profusion of towers, lanterns and spires; spires and spires sometimes were seventy meters high. <a href="/wiki/Bayeux_Cathedral" title="Bayeux Cathedral">Bayeux Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rouen_Cathedral" title="Rouen Cathedral">Rouen Cathedral</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coutances_Cathedral" title="Coutances Cathedral">Coutances Cathedral</a> are notable examples of Norman Gothic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenzler201839–41_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenzler201839–41-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Burgundy" title="Burgundy">Burgundy</a>, which had a long <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanesque style">Romanesque style</a> tradition, a <a href="/wiki/Lantern_tower" title="Lantern tower">lantern tower</a> was often included, and cathedrals often had a narrow passage the length of the cathedral at the level of the stained glass windows. as in <a href="/wiki/Auxerre_Cathedral" title="Auxerre Cathedral">Auxerre Cathedral</a>.
</p><p>In the Southwest of France, the walls were thicker, with narrow openings, and doubled with arches. The flying buttress were rarely used, replaced by heavy abutments with chapels between.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenzler201839–41_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenzler201839–41-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The south of France had its own distinct variation of the Gothic style&#160;: the <a href="/wiki/Southern_French_Gothic" title="Southern French Gothic">Southern French Gothic</a>. The Gothic cathedrals were often built with brick and tile rather than stone. They generally had thick walls and narrow windows, and were braced by heavy abutments rather than flying buttresses. The form of the tower of <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Saint-Sernin,_Toulouse" title="Basilica of Saint-Sernin, Toulouse">the basilica of Saint-Sernin</a> was copied by several cathedrals in the south, while the old nave of <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_Cathedral" title="Toulouse Cathedral">Toulouse Cathedral</a> (1210-1220) gave the model of the single nave which was generally used in Southern French Gothic architecture (although some churches had two or three naves of equal height). Some Gothic cathedrals in the Midi took unusual form; the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Albi" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of Albi">Cathedral of Albi</a> (1282–1480) was originally built as fortress, then converted to a cathedral. Albi Cathedral has another very distinctive feature; a colorful interior and painted ceiling.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenzler201839–41_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenzler201839–41-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Jacobins" title="Church of the Jacobins">Jacobins church</a> of <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, the grafting of a single apse of polygonal plan on a church with two vessels gave birth to a starry vault whose complex organization anticipated more than a century on the flamboyant Gothic. Tradition refers to this masterpiece as "palm tree", because the veins gush out of the smooth shaft of the column like palm trees.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The facade of <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_Cathedral" title="Toulouse Cathedral">Toulouse Cathedral</a> is unusual; it is the combination of two unfinished cathedral buildings, begun in the 13th century and finally put together. Toulouse Cathedral has no flying buttresses; it is supported by massive <i>contreforts</i> the height of the building, with chapels between.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English_Gothic">English Gothic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: English Gothic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/English_Gothic_architecture" title="English Gothic architecture">English Gothic architecture</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 188.66666666667px"><div style="width: 188.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 186.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar,_Gloucestershire,_UK_-_Diliff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar%2C_Gloucestershire%2C_UK_-_Diliff.jpg/280px-Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar%2C_Gloucestershire%2C_UK_-_Diliff.jpg" decoding="async" width="187" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar%2C_Gloucestershire%2C_UK_-_Diliff.jpg/421px-Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar%2C_Gloucestershire%2C_UK_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar%2C_Gloucestershire%2C_UK_-_Diliff.jpg/560px-Gloucester_Cathedral_High_Altar%2C_Gloucestershire%2C_UK_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8000" data-file-height="6430" /></a></div></div>

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 202px"><div style="width: 202px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 200px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_abbey16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Westminster_abbey16.jpg/300px-Westminster_abbey16.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Westminster_abbey16.jpg/451px-Westminster_abbey16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Westminster_abbey16.jpg/600px-Westminster_abbey16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Fan vaults with pendants at the <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_Chapel" title="Henry VII Chapel">Henry VII Chapel</a> of <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> (<a href="/wiki/Perpendicular_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Perpendicular Gothic">Perpendicular Gothic</a>) (1503)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>The Gothic style was imported very early into England, in part due to the close connection with the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Normandy" title="Duchy of Normandy">Duchy of Normandy</a>, which until 1204 was still ruled by the Kings of England. The first period is generally called <a href="/wiki/Early_English_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Early English Gothic">early English Gothic</a>, and was dominant from about 1180 to 1275. The first part of major English cathedral to feature the new style was the choir of <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_Cathedral" title="Canterbury Cathedral">Canterbury Cathedral</a>, begun about 1175. It was created by a French master builder, <a href="/wiki/William_of_Sens" title="William of Sens">William of Sens</a>. He added several original touches, including colored marble pavement, double columns in the arcades, and engaged slender <i>colonettes</i> which reached up to the vaults, borrowed from the design of <a href="/wiki/Laon_Cathedral" title="Laon Cathedral">Laon Cathedral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale199334–35_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale199334–35-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> was rebuilt from 1245 to 1517. <a href="/wiki/Salisbury_Cathedral" title="Salisbury Cathedral">Salisbury Cathedral</a> (1220–1320) is also a good example of early Gothic, with the exception of its tower and spire, which were added in 1320.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198862_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198862-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The second period of English Gothic is known as <a href="/wiki/Decorated_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Decorated Gothic">Decorated Gothic</a>. It is customarily divided into two the "Geometric" style (1250–90) and the "Curvilinear" style (1290–1350), and it is similar to the French <a href="/wiki/Rayonnant" title="Rayonnant">Rayonnant</a> style, with an emphasis on curvilinear forms, particularly in the windows. This period saw detailed stone carving reach its peak, with elaborately carved windows and <a href="/wiki/Capital_(architecture)" title="Capital (architecture)">capitals</a>, often with floral patterns, or with an accolade, a carved arch over a window decorated with pinnacles and a <a href="/wiki/Fleuron_(architecture)" title="Fleuron (architecture)">fleuron</a>, or carved floral element.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198862_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198862-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The rib vaults of the Decorated Gothic became extremely ornate, with a profusion of ribs which were purely ornamental. The vaults were often decorated with hanging stone pendants. The columns also became more ornamental, as at Peterborough Cathedral, with ribs spreading upward.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198862_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198862-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Perpendicular Gothic">Perpendicular Gothic</a> (c. 1380–1520) was final phase of English Gothic, lasting into the 16th century. As the name suggests, its emphasis was on clear horizontal and vertical lines, meeting at right angles. Columns extended upwards all the way to the roof, giving the interior the appearance of a cage of glass and stone, as in the nave of <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Cathedral" title="Gloucester Cathedral">Gloucester Cathedral</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Tudor_Arch" class="mw-redirect" title="Tudor Arch">Tudor Arch</a> appeared, wider and lower and often framed by moldings, which was used to create larger windows and to balance the strong vertical elements. The design of the rib vaults became even more complex, including the <a href="/wiki/Fan_vault" title="Fan vault">fan vault</a> with pendants used in the Henry VII chapel at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> (1503–07).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198862_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198862-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BF_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BF-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CT_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CT-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A distinctive characteristic of English cathedrals is their extreme length, and their internal emphasis upon the horizontal, which may be emphasised visually as much or more than the vertical lines. Each English cathedral (with the exception of Salisbury) has an extraordinary degree of stylistic diversity, when compared with most French, German and Italian cathedrals. It is not unusual for every part of the building to have been built in a different century and in a different style, with no attempt at creating a stylistic unity. Unlike French cathedrals, English cathedrals sprawl across their sites, with double transepts projecting strongly and <i>Lady Chapels</i> tacked on at a later date, such as at Westminster Abbey. In the west front, the doors are not as significant as in France, the usual congregational entrance being through a side porch. The West window is very large and never a rose, which are reserved for the transept gables. The west front may have two towers like a French Cathedral, or none. There is nearly always a tower at the crossing and it may be very large and surmounted by a spire. The distinctive English east end is square, but it may take a completely different form. Both internally and externally, the stonework is often richly decorated with carvings, particularly the capitals.<sup id="cite_ref-BF_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BF-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CT_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CT-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_European_Gothic">Northern European Gothic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Northern European Gothic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Germany" title="Architecture of Germany">Architecture of Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brabantine_Gothic" title="Brabantine Gothic">Brabantine Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Gothic_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Gothic architecture">Polish Gothic architecture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Czech_Gothic_architecture" title="Czech Gothic architecture">Czech Gothic architecture</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 222.66666666667px"><div style="width: 222.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 220.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kdom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Kdom.jpg/331px-Kdom.jpg" decoding="async" width="221" height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Kdom.jpg/497px-Kdom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Kdom.jpg/663px-Kdom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2318" data-file-height="1889" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Rear of <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (1248–1473)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 108px"><div style="width: 108px">

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Between the 13th and 16th centuries, Gothic cathedrals were constructed in most of the major cities of northern Europe. For the most part, they followed the French model, but with variations depending upon local traditions and the materials available. The first Gothic churches in Germany were built from about 1230. They included <i><a href="/wiki/Liebfrauenkirche,_Trier" title="Liebfrauenkirche, Trier">Liebfrauenkirche</a></i> ( ca. 1233–1283) in <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">Trier</a>, claimed to be the oldest Gothic church in Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Freiburg_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Freiburg Cathedral">Freiburg Cathedral</a>, which was built in three stages, the first beginning in 1120, though only the foundations of the original cathedral still exist. It is noted for its 116-metre tower, the only Gothic church tower in Germany that was completed in the Middle Ages (1330).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, in the region <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, was another flourishing center for Gothic architecture. <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Bohemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles IV of Bohemia">Charles IV of Bohemia</a> was both King of Bohemia and Holy Roman Empire, and he had monumental tastes. He began construction of <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>'s <a href="/wiki/St._Vitus_Cathedral" title="St. Vitus Cathedral">St. Vitus Cathedral</a> in the Gothic style in 1344, as well as a Gothic palace, <a href="/wiki/Karl%C5%A1tejn" title="Karlštejn">Karlstein Castle</a> in Central Bohemia, and Gothic buildings for the new <a href="/wiki/Charles_University" title="Charles University">University of Prague</a>. The nave of <a href="/wiki/Prague_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Prague Cathedral">Prague Cathedral</a> featured the filet vault, a decorative type of vault in which the ribs criss-crossed in a mesh pattern, similar to the vaults of <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Cathedral" title="Bristol Cathedral">Bristol Cathedral</a> and other English churches. His other Gothic projects included the lavishly decorated Chapel of the Holy Cross inside <a href="/wiki/Karl%C5%A1tejn" title="Karlštejn">Karlstein Castle</a> (1357–1367), and the choir of <a href="/wiki/Aachen_Cathedral" title="Aachen Cathedral">Aachen Cathedral</a> begun in 1355, which was built on the model of <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Chapelle" title="Sainte-Chapelle">Sainte-Chapelle</a> in Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993221–230_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993221–230-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Gothic architecture in Germany and the kingdoms of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> generally followed the French formula, but the towers were much taller and, if completed, were often surmounted by enormous openwork spires. The distinctive character of the interior of German Gothic cathedrals is their breadth and openness. German and Czech cathedrals, like the French, tend not to have strongly projecting <a href="/wiki/Transept" title="Transept">transepts</a>. There are also many <a href="/wiki/Hall_church" title="Hall church">hall churches</a> (<i>Hallenkirchen</i>) without <a href="/wiki/Clerestory" title="Clerestory">clerestory</a> windows.<sup id="cite_ref-BF_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BF-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Swaan_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swaan-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Cathedral" title="Cologne Cathedral">Cologne Cathedral</a> is after <a href="/wiki/Milan_Cathedral" title="Milan Cathedral">Milan Cathedral</a> the largest Gothic cathedral in the world. Construction began in 1248 and took, with interruptions, until 1880 to complete&#160;– a period of over 600 years. It is 144.5 metres long, 86.5&#160;m wide and its two towers are 157&#160;m tall.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Brick_Gothic" title="Brick Gothic">Brick Gothic</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Backsteingotik</i>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Gotyk ceglany</i>) is a specific style common in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern Europe</a>, especially in Northern Germany, Poland and in the regions around the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> without natural rock resources. Prime examples of brick gothic include <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Church,_Gda%C5%84sk" title="St. Mary&#39;s Church, Gdańsk">St. Mary's Church, Gdańsk</a> (1379–1502),<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w" title="St. Mary&#39;s Basilica, Kraków">St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków</a> (1290–1365) and <a href="/wiki/Malbork_Castle" title="Malbork Castle">Malbork Castle</a> (13th century).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen&#39;s Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna</a> (1339–1365) has the distinctive feature of a polychrome roof. Another regional variation is the <a href="/wiki/Brabantine_Gothic" title="Brabantine Gothic">Brabantine Gothic</a> a style found in Belgium and the Netherlands. It is characterized by using light-colored <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> or limestone, which allowed rich detailing but was prone to erosion. Features included columns with sculpted cabbage-like foliage, arched windows whose points came right up into the vaults. and, sometimes, a wooden ceiling. Examples include <a href="/wiki/Grote_Kerk,_Haarlem" title="Grote Kerk, Haarlem">Grote Kerk, Haarlem</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Haarlem" title="Haarlem">Haarlem</a>, the Netherlands, originally built as a Catholic Cathedral, now a Protestant church, and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Blessed_Lady_of_the_Sablon" title="Church of Our Blessed Lady of the Sablon">Church of Our Blessed Lady of the Sablon</a> in Brussels (15th century).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_European_Gothic">Southern European Gothic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Southern European Gothic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain_and_Portugal">Spain and Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Spain and Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Gothic nave of <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vora_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Évora Cathedral">Évora Cathedral</a>, Portugal, leads to a <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> chapel (1280–1340)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>Strikingly different variations of the Gothic style appeared in southern Europe, particularly in Spain and Portugal. Important examples of Spanish Gothic include <a href="/wiki/Toledo_Cathedral" title="Toledo Cathedral">Toledo Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_Cathedral" title="León Cathedral">León Cathedral</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Burgos_Cathedral" title="Burgos Cathedral">Burgos Cathedral</a>.
The distinctive characteristic of Gothic cathedrals of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> is their spatial complexity, with many areas of different shapes leading from each other. They are comparatively wide, and often have very tall arcades surmounted by low clerestories, giving a similar spacious appearance to the <i>Hallenkirche</i> of Germany, as at the Church of the <a href="/wiki/Batalha_Monastery" title="Batalha Monastery">Batalha Monastery</a> in Portugal. Many of the cathedrals are completely surrounded by chapels. Like English cathedrals, each is often stylistically diverse. This expresses itself both in the addition of chapels and in the application of decorative details drawn from different sources. Among the influences on both decoration and form are <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architecture</a> and, towards the end of the period, Renaissance details combined with the Gothic in a distinctive manner. The West front, as at <a href="/wiki/Leon_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Leon Cathedral">Leon Cathedral</a>, typically resembles a French west front, but wider in proportion to height and often with greater diversity of detail and a combination of intricate ornament with broad plain surfaces. At <a href="/wiki/Burgos_Cathedral" title="Burgos Cathedral">Burgos Cathedral</a> there are spires of German style. The roofline often has pierced parapets with comparatively few pinnacles. There are often towers and domes of a great variety of shapes and structural invention rising above the roof.<sup id="cite_ref-BF_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BF-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the territories under the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a> (Aragon, Catalonia, <a href="/wiki/Roussillon" title="Roussillon">Roussillon</a> in France, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian Community</a>, among others in the Italian islands), the Gothic style suppressed the <a href="/wiki/Transept" title="Transept">transept</a> and made the <a href="/wiki/Aisle#Church_architecture" title="Aisle">side-aisles</a> almost as high as the main nave, creating wider spaces, and with few ornaments. There are two different Gothic styles in the Aragonese lands: <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Gothic" title="Catalan Gothic">Catalan Gothic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Gothic" title="Valencian Gothic">Valencian Gothic</a>, which are different from those in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a> and France.
</p><p>The most important samples of Catalan Gothic style are the cathedrals of <a href="/wiki/Girona" title="Girona">Girona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perpignan" title="Perpignan">Perpignan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palma,_Majorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Palma, Majorca">Palma</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Mallorca" title="Mallorca">Mallorca</a>), the basilica of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Mar,_Barcelona" title="Santa Maria del Mar, Barcelona">Santa Maria del Mar</a> (in Barcelona), the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Pi,_Barcelona" title="Santa Maria del Pi, Barcelona">Basílica del Pi</a> (in Barcelona), and the church of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria,_Manresa" title="Santa Maria, Manresa">Santa Maria de l'Alba</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manresa" title="Manresa">Manresa</a>.
</p><p>The most important examples of Valencian Gothic style in the old <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">Kingdom of Valencia</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Cathedral" title="Valencia Cathedral">Valencia Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llotja_de_la_Seda" title="Llotja de la Seda">Llotja de la Seda</a> (Unesco World Heritage site), <a href="/wiki/Torres_de_Serranos" title="Torres de Serranos">Torres de Serranos</a>, Torres de Quart, <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_Sant_Jeroni_de_Cotalba" title="Monastery of Sant Jeroni de Cotalba">Monastery of Sant Jeroni de Cotalba</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Alfauir" title="Alfauir">Alfauir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Borgias" title="Palace of the Borgias">Palace of the Borgias</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gandia" title="Gandia">Gandia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_la_Valldigna" title="Monastery of Santa María de la Valldigna">Monastery of Santa María de la Valldigna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Santa_Maria,_Alicante" title="Basilica of Santa Maria, Alicante">Basilica of Santa Maria</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">Alicante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orihuela_Cathedral" title="Orihuela Cathedral">Orihuela Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castell%C3%B3_Cathedral" title="Castelló Cathedral">Castelló Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Fadr%C3%AD" title="El Fadrí">El Fadrí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Segorbe_Cathedral" title="Segorbe Cathedral">Segorbe Cathedral</a>, etc.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><a href="/wiki/Italian_Gothic_architecture" title="Italian Gothic architecture">Italian Gothic architecture</a> went its own particular way, departing from the French model. It was influenced by other styles, notably the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine style">Byzantine style</a> introduced in <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">Ravenna</a>. Major examples include <a href="/wiki/Milan_Cathedral" title="Milan Cathedral">Milan Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Orvieto_Cathedral" title="Orvieto Cathedral">Orvieto Cathedral</a>, and particularly <a href="/wiki/Florence_Cathedral" title="Florence Cathedral">Florence Cathedral</a>, before the addition of the Duomo in the Renaissance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198862_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198862-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Italian style was influenced by the materials available in the different regions; <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a> was available in great quantities in <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a>, and was lavishly used in churches; it was scarce in <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombardy</a>, and brick was used instead. But many of the architectural elements were used apparently mainly to be different from the French style.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993147_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993147-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cistercian" class="mw-redirect" title="Cistercian">Cistercian</a> monastic order introduced some of the first Gothic churches into Italy, in <a href="/wiki/Fossanova_Abbey" title="Fossanova Abbey">Fossanova Abbey</a> (consecrated 1208) and the <a href="/wiki/Casamari_Abbey" title="Casamari Abbey">Casamari Abbey</a> (1203–1217). They followed the basic plan of the Gothic Cistercian churches of <a href="/wiki/Burgundy" title="Burgundy">Burgundy</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/C%C3%AEteaux_Abbey" title="Cîteaux Abbey">Cîteaux Abbey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993148_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993148-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Italian plan is usually regular and symmetrical, Italian cathedrals have few and widely spaced columns. The proportions are generally mathematically equilibrated, based on the square and the concept of "<i>armonìa</i>", and except in Venice where they loved flamboyant arches, the arches are almost always equilateral. Italian Gothic cathedrals often retained Romanesque features; the nave of <a href="/wiki/Orvieto_Cathedral" title="Orvieto Cathedral">Orvieto Cathedral</a> had Romanesque arches and vaults.
</p><p>Italian Cathedrals also offered a variety of plans; <a href="/wiki/Florence_Cathedral" title="Florence Cathedral">Florence Cathedral</a> (begun 1246) had a rectangular choir, based on the Cistercian model, but was designed to have three wings with polygonal chapels. Italian Gothic cathedrals were general not as tall as those in France; they rarely used flying buttresses, and generally had only two levels, an arcade and a claire-voie with small windows; but <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Cathedral" title="Bologna Cathedral">Bologna Cathedral</a> (begun in 1388), rivaled <a href="/wiki/Bourges_Cathedral" title="Bourges Cathedral">Bourges Cathedral</a> in France in height. The smallest notable Italian Gothic church is <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_della_Spina" title="Santa Maria della Spina">Santa Maria della Spina</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a> (about 1330), which resembles a Gothic jewel box.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993148_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993148-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A distinctive characteristic of Italian Gothic is the use of polychrome decoration, both externally as marble veneer on the brick façade and internally where the arches are often made of alternating black and white segments. The columns were sometimes painted red, and the walls were decorated with frescoes and the apse with mosaic. Italian cathedral façades are often polychrome and may include mosaics in the lunettes over the doors. The façades have projecting open porches and ocular or wheel windows rather than roses, and do not usually have a tower. The crossing is usually surmounted by a dome. There is often a free-standing tower and baptistery. The eastern end usually has an apse of comparatively low projection. The windows are not as large as in northern Europe and, although stained glass windows are often found, the favourite narrative medium for the interior is the <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">fresco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BF_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BF-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The facade of <a href="/wiki/Orvieto_Cathedral" title="Orvieto Cathedral">Orvieto Cathedral</a>, begun in 1310, is a striking example of mosaic decoration. Another innovation of Italian Gothic is the bronze doorway covered with sculpture; the most famous examples are the doors of the Baptistry of Florence, by <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Pisano" title="Andrea Pisano">Andrea Pisano</a> (1330–1336).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993161–175_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993161–175-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Italian Gothic cathedrals did not have the elaborate sculptural tympanums over the entrances of French cathedrals, but they had abundant realistic sculptural decoration. Some of the finest work was done by <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Pisano" title="Nicola Pisano">Nicola Pisano</a> at the Baptistery of <a href="/wiki/Pisa_Cathedral" title="Pisa Cathedral">Pisa Cathedral</a> (1259–60), and in <a href="/wiki/Siena_Cathedral" title="Siena Cathedral">Siena Cathedral</a>; and by his son <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Pisano" title="Giovanni Pisano">Giovanni Pisano</a> on the west facade of Pisa Cathedral (1284–85).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993152–176_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartindale1993152–176-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gothic_in_the_Colonial_Americas">Gothic in the Colonial Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Gothic in the Colonial Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 268.66666666667px"><div style="width: 268.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 266.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg/400px-Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="267" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg/600px-Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg/800px-Palacio_de_Cort%C3%A9s_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Cort%C3%A9s,_Cuernavaca" title="Palace of Cortés, Cuernavaca">Palace of Cortés</a> (1523-1528) in Cuernavaca, Mexico, this palace has a style that blends Gothic and <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar_art" title="Mudéjar art">Mudéjar</a><sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 300.66666666667px"><div style="width: 300.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 298.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg/448px-20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg" decoding="async" width="299" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg/672px-20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg/897px-20090405-182346-_eglise_du_couvent_saint_gabriel_-modifi%C3%A9e-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/San_Gabriel_Franciscan_Convent,_Cholula" title="San Gabriel Franciscan Convent, Cholula">San Gabriel Franciscan Convent</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cholula,_Puebla" title="Cholula, Puebla">Cholula</a>, Metropolitan area of Puebla City, Mexico, it is partially Gothic (built in the mid-16th century)<sup id="cite_ref-lonelyplanet.com/mexico_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lonelyplanet.com/mexico-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-inafed.gob.mx_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inafed.gob.mx-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 302px"><div style="width: 302px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 300px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG/450px-Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG/675px-Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG/900px-Templo_y_convento_de_San_Mateo_Ap%C3%B3stol.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Earliest_16th-century_monasteries_on_the_slopes_of_Popocat%C3%A9petl" title="Earliest 16th-century monasteries on the slopes of Popocatépetl">Convent of San Mateo Apóstol y Evangelista</a> (1535-1567)<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Atlatlahucan" title="Atlatlahucan">Atlatlahucan</a>, Mexico, is a late-Gothic <a href="/wiki/Plateresque" title="Plateresque">Plateresque</a> church that is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a><sup id="cite_ref-list/702_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-list/702-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>There are late-Gothic architecture from the era in some of the oldest Christian churches built in the Americas. Few examples can be mentioned as the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_Cathedral_of_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_la_Menor" title="Basilica Cathedral of Santa María la Menor">Basilica Cathedral of Santa María la Menor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> built between 1514-1541, the building is mainly Gothic<sup id="cite_ref-5albemarleway.co.uk_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5albemarleway.co.uk-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-whc.unesco.org_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whc.unesco.org-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and is the oldest cathedral in the Americas;<sup id="cite_ref-whc.unesco.org_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whc.unesco.org-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Mexico City Metropolitan Cathedral">Mexico City Metropolitan Cathedral</a>, started to built in 1573,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> which retains Gothic elements as the two <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vaults</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sacristy" title="Sacristy">sacristy</a> and the vaults covering the <a href="/wiki/Chapter_house" title="Chapter house">chapter house</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-catedralmetropolitanademexico.mx_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catedralmetropolitanademexico.mx-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Other example is the <a href="/wiki/San_Gabriel_Franciscan_Convent,_Cholula" title="San Gabriel Franciscan Convent, Cholula">San Gabriel Franciscan Convent</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cholula,_Puebla" title="Cholula, Puebla">Cholula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area_of_Puebla" title="Metropolitan area of Puebla">Metropolitan area of Puebla</a>, Mexico, the exterior and interior are partially Gothic<sup id="cite_ref-lonelyplanet.com/mexico_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lonelyplanet.com/mexico-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-inafed.gob.mx_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inafed.gob.mx-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> although the tower is Baroque, was built between 1540s-1550s. In the field of the Civil Gothic architecture, a notable example is the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Cort%C3%A9s,_Cuernavaca" title="Palace of Cortés, Cuernavaca">Palace of Cortés</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a>, Mexico, built between 1523-1528,<sup id="cite_ref-Routledge_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Routledge-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> is the oldest conserved Colonial-era civil structure in the continental Americas, the palace has a style that blends Gothic and <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar_art" title="Mudéjar art">Mudéjar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is also many late-Gothic <a href="/wiki/Plateresque" title="Plateresque">Plateresque</a> architecture throughout Mexican territory. Also there are several churches of the <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by UNESCO with the name <a href="/wiki/Earliest_16th-century_monasteries_on_the_slopes_of_Popocat%C3%A9petl" title="Earliest 16th-century monasteries on the slopes of Popocatépetl">Earliest 16th-century monasteries on the slopes of Popocatépetl</a> that are Plateresque Gothics.<sup id="cite_ref-list/702_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-list/702-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Abbeys_and_monasteries">Abbeys and monasteries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Abbeys and monasteries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 234.66666666667px"><div style="width: 234.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 232.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg/349px-Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="233" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg/525px-Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg/700px-Abbaye_Saint-Ouen_de_Rouen_as_seen_from_Gros_Horloge_140215_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5313" data-file-height="3985" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Ouen,_Rouen" title="Church of St. Ouen, Rouen">Abbey of Saint-Ouen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rouen" title="Rouen">Rouen</a> (1318–1537)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 248.66666666667px"><div style="width: 248.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 246.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg/370px-FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg" decoding="async" width="247" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg/556px-FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg/741px-FranceNormandieLeMontSaintMichelAbbaye.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2534" data-file-height="1795" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Mont_Saint_Michel_Abbey" class="mw-redirect" title="Mont Saint Michel Abbey">Mont Saint Michel Abbey</a> church (Choir completed 1228)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 246.66666666667px"><div style="width: 246.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 244.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg/367px-Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg" decoding="async" width="245" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg/552px-Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg/735px-Reims_SRemi1_tango7174.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="714" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Abbey_of_Saint-Remi" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbey of Saint-Remi">Abbey of Saint-Remi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a> (1170–80)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 322.66666666667px"><div style="width: 322.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 320.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalha_monastery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Batalha_monastery.jpg/481px-Batalha_monastery.jpg" decoding="async" width="321" height="176" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Batalha_monastery.jpg/723px-Batalha_monastery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Batalha_monastery.jpg/963px-Batalha_monastery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3672" data-file-height="2003" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Batalha_Monastery" title="Batalha Monastery">Batalha Monastery</a>, Portugal (1386–1517)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>While cathedrals were the most prominent structures in the Gothic style, Gothic features were also built for many monasteries across Europe. Prominent examples were built by the <a href="/wiki/Benedictine_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine order">Benedictines</a> in England, France, and Normandy. They were the builders of the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St_Denis" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of St Denis">Abbey of St Denis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Abbey_of_Saint-Remi" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbey of Saint-Remi">Abbey of Saint-Remi</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. Later Benedictine projects (constructions and renovations) include <a href="/wiki/Rouen" title="Rouen">Rouen</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Ouen,_Rouen" title="Church of St. Ouen, Rouen">Abbey of Saint-Ouen</a>, the Abbey <a href="/wiki/La_Chaise-Dieu" title="La Chaise-Dieu">La Chaise-Dieu</a>, and the choir of <a href="/wiki/Mont_Saint-Michel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mont Saint-Michel">Mont Saint-Michel</a> in France.
</p><p>English examples are <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>, originally built as a <a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> order monastic church; and the reconstruction of <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_Cathedral" title="Canterbury Cathedral">the Benedictine church at</a> <a href="/wiki/Canterbury" title="Canterbury">Canterbury</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cistercian_Order" class="mw-redirect" title="Cistercian Order">Cistercians</a> spread the style as far east and south as <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrodecki197728_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrodecki197728-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Smaller orders such as the <a href="/wiki/Carthusian_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthusian order">Carthusians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Premonstratensians" title="Premonstratensians">Premonstratensians</a> also built some 200 churches, usually near cities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrodecki197729–30_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrodecki197729–30-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Franciscans" title="Franciscans">Franciscans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominicans</a> also carried out a transition to Gothic in the 13th and 14th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Order</a>, a military order, spread Gothic art into <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a>, and the Baltic region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrodecki197730_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrodecki197730-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest example of Gothic architecture in Germany is <a href="/wiki/Maulbronn_Monastery" title="Maulbronn Monastery">Maulbronn Monastery</a>, a Romanesque <a href="/wiki/Cistercian" class="mw-redirect" title="Cistercian">Cistercian</a> abbey in southwest Germany whose <a href="/wiki/Narthex" title="Narthex">narthex</a> was built in the early 12th century by an anonymous architect.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurtonKerr201179_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurtonKerr201179-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Batalha_Monastery" title="Batalha Monastery">Batalha Monastery</a> (1386–1517) is a Dominican monastery in <a href="/wiki/Batalha,_Portugal" title="Batalha, Portugal">Batalha, Portugal</a>. The monastery was built in the <a href="/wiki/Flamboyant_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Flamboyant Gothic">Flamboyant Gothic</a> style to thank the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a> for the Portuguese victory over the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aljubarrota" title="Battle of Aljubarrota">Battle of Aljubarrota</a> in 1385.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civic_architecture">Civic architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Civic architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 300px"><div style="width: 300px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 298px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg/447px-Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg" decoding="async" width="298" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg/670px-Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg/894px-Palais_de_la_Cite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1127" data-file-height="757" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Palais_de_la_Cit%C3%A9" title="Palais de la Cité">Palais de la Cité</a> in Paris (begun 1119) which included the royal residence and later <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Chapelle" title="Sainte-Chapelle">Sainte-Chapelle</a> (1238–1248)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 268.66666666667px"><div style="width: 268.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 266.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG/400px-Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG" decoding="async" width="267" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG/600px-Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG/800px-Conciergerie_Salle_des_gens_d%27armes_11.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a></div></div>

</p>

		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 267.33333333333px"><div style="width: 267.33333333333px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 265.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg/398px-Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg" decoding="async" width="266" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg/597px-Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg/797px-Fa%C3%A7ade_du_Palais_des_Papes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="969" data-file-height="730" /></a></div></div>

			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 268.66666666667px"><div style="width: 268.66666666667px">

</p>
			</div>

</ul>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gothic_secular_and_domestic_architecture" title="Gothic secular and domestic architecture">Gothic secular and domestic architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">Castle</a></div>
<p>The Gothic style appeared in palaces in France, including the Papal Palace in Avignon and the <a href="/wiki/Palais_de_la_Cit%C3%A9" title="Palais de la Cité">Palais de la Cité</a> in Paris, close to <a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre-Dame de Paris">Notre-Dame de Paris</a>, begun in 1119, which was the principal residence of the French Kings until 1417. Most of the Palais de la Cité is gone, but two of the original towers along the Seine, of the towers, the vaulted ceilings of the Hall of the Men-at-Arms (1302), (now in the <a href="/wiki/Conciergerie" title="Conciergerie">Conciergerie</a>; and the original chapel, <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Chapelle" title="Sainte-Chapelle">Sainte-Chapelle</a>, can still be seen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETexier201212_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETexier201212-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest civic building built in the Gothic style in France was the <a href="/wiki/Palais_des_Papes" title="Palais des Papes">Palais des Papes</a> (Palace of the Popes) constructed between 1252 and 1364, when the Popes fled the political chaos and wars enveloping Rome. Given the complicated political situation, it combined the functions of a church, a seat of government and a fortress.
</p><p>In the 15th century, following the late Gothic or flamboyant period, elements of Gothic decoration borrowed from cathedrals began to appear in the town halls of northern France, in Flanders and in the Netherlands. The Hôtel de Ville of <a href="/wiki/Compi%C3%A8gne" title="Compiègne">Compiègne</a> has an imposing gothic bell tower, featuring a spire surrounded by smaller towers, and its windows are decorated with ornate <i>accolades</i> or ornamental arches. Similarly flamboyant town halls were found in <a href="/wiki/Arras" title="Arras">Arras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douai" title="Douai">Douai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Quentin,_Aisne" title="Saint-Quentin, Aisne">Saint-Quentin, Aisne</a>, and in modern Belgium, in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198864_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198864-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Notable Gothic civil architecture in Spain includes the <a href="/wiki/Llotja_de_la_Seda" title="Llotja de la Seda">Silk Exchange</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>, Spain (1482–1548), a major marketplace, which features a main hall with twisting columns beneath its vaulted ceiling. Another Spanish Gothic landmark is the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Kings_of_Navarre_of_Olite" title="Palace of the Kings of Navarre of Olite">Palace of the Kings of Navarre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Olite" title="Olite">Olite</a> (1269–1512), which combining the features of a palace and a fortress.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_Gothic">University Gothic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: University Gothic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic">Collegiate Gothic</a></div>

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>The first universities in Europe were closely associated with the Catholic church, and in the late 15th century they adapted variations of the Gothic style for their architecture. The Gothic style was adapted from English monasteries for use in the first colleges of <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Magdalen College">Magdalen College</a>. It was also used at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Salamanca" title="University of Salamanca">University of Salamanca</a> in Spain. The use of the late Gothic style at Oxford and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a> inspired the picturesque Gothic architecture in U.S. colleges in the 19th and 20th century.
</p><p>By the late Middle Ages university towns had grown in wealth and importance as well, and this was reflected in the buildings of some of Europe's ancient universities. Particularly remarkable examples still standing nowadays include the <a href="/wiki/Collegio_di_Spagna" title="Collegio di Spagna">Collegio di Spagna</a> in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a>, built during the 14th and 15th centuries; the <a href="/wiki/Karolinum" title="Karolinum">Collegium Carolinum</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_University_in_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles University in Prague">Charles University in Prague</a> in Bohemia; the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Salamanca" title="University of Salamanca">Escuelas mayores</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Salamanca" title="University of Salamanca">University of Salamanca</a> in Spain; the chapel of <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="King&#39;s College, Cambridge">King's College, Cambridge</a>; or the <a href="/wiki/Collegium_Maius" title="Collegium Maius">Collegium Maius</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Jagiellonian University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, Poland.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_architecture">Military architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Military architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

			<div class="thumb" style="width: 266.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:2012.05.12_MALBORK_(4).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2012.05.12_MALBORK_%284%29.JPG/400px-2012.05.12_MALBORK_%284%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="267" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2012.05.12_MALBORK_%284%29.JPG/600px-2012.05.12_MALBORK_%284%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2012.05.12_MALBORK_%284%29.JPG/800px-2012.05.12_MALBORK_%284%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a></div></div>

<p><a href="/wiki/Malbork_Castle" title="Malbork Castle">Malbork Castle</a> in Poland (13th century)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 300px"><div style="width: 300px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 298px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg/447px-Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg" decoding="async" width="298" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg/671px-Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg/894px-Exterior_Alcazar_Segovia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1074" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Alcazar_of_Segovia" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcazar of Segovia">Alcazar of Segovia</a> (12th–13th centuries)
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 268.66666666667px"><div style="width: 268.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 266.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG/400px-Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG" decoding="async" width="267" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG/600px-Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG/800px-Burg_Hohenzollern.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern Castle</a> (1454–1461) in <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, southern Germany
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<p>In the 13th century, the design of the <i>chateau fort</i>, or castle, was modified, based on the Byzantine and Moslem castles the French knights had seen during the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a>. The new kind of fortification was called Phillipienne, after <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Auguste" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippe Auguste">Philippe Auguste</a>, who had taken part in the Crusades. The new fortifications were more geometric, usually square, with a high main <i>donjon</i> or tower, in the center, which could be defended even if the walls of the castle were captured. The Donjon of the <a href="/wiki/Chateau_de_Vincennes" class="mw-redirect" title="Chateau de Vincennes">Chateau de Vincennes</a>, begun by <a href="/wiki/Philip_VI_of_France" title="Philip VI of France">Philip VI of France</a>, was a good example. It was 52 meters high, the tallest military tower in Europe.
</p><p>In the Phillipienne castle other towers, usually round were placed at the corners and along the walls, close enough together to support each other. The walls had two levels of walkways on the inside, an upper parapet with openings (<i>Crénaux</i>) from which soldiers could watch or fire arrows on besiegers below; narrow openings (<i>Merlons</i>) through which they could be sheltered as they fired arrows; and floor openings (<i>Mâchicoulis</i>), from which they could drop rocks, burning oil or other objects on the besiegers. The upper walls also had protected protruding balconies, <i>Échauguettes</i> and <i>Bretéches</i>, from which soldiers could see what was happening at the corners or on the ground below. In addition, the towers and walls were pierced with narrow vertical slits, called <i>Meurtriéres</i>, through which archers could fire arrows. In later castles the slits took the form of crosses, so that archers could fire <i>arbalètes</i>, or <a href="/wiki/Crossbows" class="mw-redirect" title="Crossbows">crossbows</a>, in different directions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDucher198866–67_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDucher198866–67-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Castles were surrounded by deep moat, spanned by a single drawbridge. The entrance was also protected by a grill of iron which could be opened and closed. The walls at the bottom were often sloping, and protected with earthen barriers. One good surviving example is the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Dourdan" title="Château de Dourdan">Château de Dourdan</a> in the Seine-et-Marne department, near <a href="/wiki/Nemours" title="Nemours">Nemours</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the end of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a> (1337–1453), with improvements in artillery, the castles lost most of their military importance. They remained as symbols of the rank of their noble occupants; the narrowing openings in the walls were often widened into the windows of bedchambers and ceremonial halls. The tower of the Chateau of Vincennes became a royal residence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERenaultLazé200638_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERenaultLazé200638-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Beginning in the 16th century, as <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance architecture</a> from Italy began to appear in France and other countries in Europe, the dominance of Gothic architecture began to wane. Nonetheless, new Gothic buildings, particularly churches, continued to be built; new Gothic churches built in Paris in this period included <a href="/wiki/Saint-Merri" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-Merri">Saint-Merri</a> (1520–1552); and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Germain-l%27Auxerrois" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-Germain-l&#39;Auxerrois">Saint-Germain-l'Auxerrois</a>; The first signs of classicism in Paris churches, at <a href="/wiki/St-Gervais-et-St-Protais" title="St-Gervais-et-St-Protais">St-Gervais-et-St-Protais</a>, did not appear until 1540. The largest new church, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Eustache,_Paris" title="Saint-Eustache, Paris">Saint-Eustache</a> (1532–1560), rivaled Notre-Dame in size, 105 meters long, 44 meters wide, and 35 meters high. As construction of this church continued, elements of Renaissance decoration, including the system of classical orders of columns, were added to the design, making it an early Gothic-Renaissance hybrid.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETexier201224–26_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETexier201224–26-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Gothic style began to be described as outdated, ugly and even barbaric. The term "Gothic" was first used as a <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a> description. <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Vasari" title="Giorgio Vasari">Giorgio Vasari</a> used the term "barbarous German style" in his 1550 <i><a href="/wiki/Lives_of_the_Most_Excellent_Painters,_Sculptors,_and_Architects" title="Lives of the Most Excellent Painters, Sculptors, and Architects">Lives of the Artists</a></i> to describe what is now considered the Gothic style.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVasari1991117,_527_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVasari1991117,_527-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In the introduction to the <i>Lives</i> he attributed various architectural features to "<a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">the Goths</a>" whom he held responsible for destroying the ancient buildings after they conquered <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, and erecting new ones in this style.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVasariBrownMaclehose190783_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVasariBrownMaclehose190783-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In the 17th century, <a href="/wiki/Moli%C3%A8re" title="Molière">Molière</a> also mocked the Gothic style in the 1669 poem <i>La Gloire</i>: "...the insipid taste of Gothic ornamentation, these odious monstrosities of an ignorant age, produced by the torrents of barbarism..."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrodecki19779_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrodecki19779-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The dominant styles in Europe became in turn <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Renaissance architecture">Italian Renaissance architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a>, and the grand classicism of the <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV style">Louis XIV style</a>.
</p><p>Nonetheless, Gothic architecture, usually churches or university buildings, continued to be built. Ireland was an island of Gothic architecture in the 17th and 18th centuries, with the construction of <a href="/wiki/St_Columb%27s_Cathedral" title="St Columb&#39;s Cathedral">Derry Cathedral</a> (completed 1633), <a href="/wiki/St_John_the_Baptist_Cathedral,_Sligo" title="St John the Baptist Cathedral, Sligo">Sligo Cathedral</a> (c. 1730), and <a href="/wiki/Down_Cathedral" title="Down Cathedral">Down Cathedral</a> (1790–1818) are other notable examples.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In the 17th and 18th century several important Gothic buildings were constructed at <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge University">Cambridge University</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Tom_Tower" title="Tom Tower">Tom Tower</a> at <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford" title="Christ Church, Oxford">Christ Church, Oxford</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">Christopher Wren</a> (1681–82) It also appeared, in a whimsical fashion, in <a href="/wiki/Horace_Walpole" title="Horace Walpole">Horace Walpole</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Twickenham" title="Twickenham">Twickenham</a> <a href="/wiki/Villa" title="Villa">villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strawberry_Hill_House" title="Strawberry Hill House">Strawberry Hill</a> (1749–1776) The two western towers of <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> were constructed between 1722 and 1745 by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Hawksmoor" title="Nicholas Hawksmoor">Nicholas Hawksmoor</a>, opening a new period of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic Revival">Gothic Revival</a>.
</p>
<h2><span id="Survival.2C_rediscovery_and_revival"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Survival,_rediscovery_and_revival">Survival, rediscovery and revival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Survival, rediscovery and revival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="England">England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothic_architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

</p>
